  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_66f1a7a7-0ce2-4275-afe9-e9e88290afbe'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer9965971899364647294">Sophos, under the guidance of yet another tutor, practices his swordplay and strategizes escape scenarios should his father's villa come under attack. How would he save his mother? His sisters? Himself? Could he reach the horses in time? Where would he go? But nothing prepares him for the day armed men, silent as thieves, swarm the villa courtyard ready to kill, to capture</span>
  <span id="freeText9965971899364647294" style="display:none">Sophos, under the guidance of yet another tutor, practices his swordplay and strategizes escape scenarios should his father's villa come under attack. How would he save his mother? His sisters? Himself? Could he reach the horses in time? Where would he go? But nothing prepares him for the day armed men, silent as thieves, swarm the villa courtyard ready to kill, to capture, to kidnap. Sophos, the heir to the throne of Sounis, disappears without a trace. <br /><br />In Attolia, Eugenides, the new and unlikely king, has never stopped wondering what happened to Sophos. Nor has the Queen of Eddis. They send spies. They pay informants. They appeal to the gods. But as time goes by, it becomes less and less certain that they will ever see their friend alive again. <br /><br />Across the small peninsula battles are fought, bribes are offered, and conspiracies are set in motion. Darkening the horizon, the Mede Empire threatens, always, from across the sea. And Sophos, anonymous and alone, bides his time. Sophos, drawing on his memories of Gen, Pol, the Magus and Eddis, sets out on an adventure that will change all of their lives forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9965971899364647294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_10454271').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_10454271').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_10454271').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script></div>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/41924159-marian-mayuga">Marian Mayuga</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I'll try my best to come up with a decent (spoiler-free) list...<br/>- It passes the Bechdel test<br/>- The story takes place in three countries, two of which a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I'll try my best to come up with a decent (spoiler-free) list...<br />- It passes the Bechdel test<br />- The story takes place in three countries, two of which are ruled by queens who insist that whoever they marry is of their own choosing<br />- Although many of the characters are male (including the protagonist), the women play roles NO LESS important<br />- But the women go about their duties not to prove anything for their gender, but simply to fulfill their responsibilities<br />- The uncontested ruler of lesser gods is a goddess named Hephestia<br />- There is no one ideal representation of women in any of the female characters; they are unique, flawed and beautiful in their own ways<br /><br />To those who've read this, please feel free to add more to this list! :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9110750481989071525">I’ve read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995733992' rel='nofollow noopener'>five</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030955705' rel='nofollow noopener'>books</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376881446' rel='nofollow noopener'>of</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2467555040' rel='nofollow noopener'>this</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484905696' rel='nofollow noopener'>now</a>, so here’s a quick roundoff of my points:<br/>✔Megan Whalen Turner is so good at planting and payoff it makes me want to cry<br/>✔I have never seen an author follow through in such interesting ways<br/>✔anyway a romantic pairing that got set up in book ONE just got payed off<br/>✔all the scenes work individually but ALSO as callbacks to earlier plot points<br/>✔she keeps pulling the rug out from under us with some huge reveal that makes you want to scream<br/>✔so many different players<br/>✔so muc</span>
  <span id="freeText9110750481989071525" style="display:none">I’ve read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995733992" rel="nofollow noopener">five</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030955705" rel="nofollow noopener">books</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376881446" rel="nofollow noopener">of</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2467555040" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484905696" rel="nofollow noopener">now</a>, so here’s a quick roundoff of my points:<br />✔Megan Whalen Turner is so good at planting and payoff it makes me want to cry<br />✔I have never seen an author follow through in such interesting ways<br />✔anyway a romantic pairing that got set up in book ONE just got payed off<br />✔all the scenes work individually but ALSO as callbacks to earlier plot points<br />✔she keeps pulling the rug out from under us with some huge reveal that makes you want to scream<br />✔so many different players<br />✔so much character development<br />✔so much dimensionality<br />✔but usually in a very good way? I’m always delighted by her plot twists<br />✔upsetting things happen but then the books as a whole are Happy And Good<br /><br />That's my full review. But also, here is a roundup of things that stood out in <i>this</i> book:<br /><blockquote>✔Everyone showed up.<br />✔No, really. Every single lead.</blockquote><br /><br />Yes, I’ve gotten through three and a half reviews without doing a character roundup, so I just had to mention the current leads of this job:<br /><br />➽<b>
  <i>Sophos</i>
</b><br />the literal epitome of haha I want to die. I actually loved his character arc so much but he’s <i>so much of a disaster</i>. <br /><br />➽<b>
  <i>Eddis</i>
</b><br />a queen and icon, but in such a dimensional way. she is not a ruthless power player <s>like my favorite female character</s>, but she still wields so much power in her own narrative. <br /><br />➽<b>
  <i>Irene</i>
</b><br />still my favorite character, but she’s not showing up as much. and it is absolutely tragic and I think she deserves to be the lead character of the final book. <br /><br />➽<b>
  <i>Gen</i>
</b><br /><b>
  <i>final side note:</i>
</b> Gen and Irene: interact with Sophos for a second<br />me: personally, I love Sophos’ parents<br />Absolutely the most hilarious protagonist I have ever come across.<br /><br />Basically, <b>I love this complete disaster of a found family of ridiculous, extra characters, and this ridiculous series of political intrigue and plot twists.</b> I cannot wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2461451115" rel="nofollow noopener">book six</a> to hurry up and release.<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

<div id="review_87920728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87920728" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87920728?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mythopoeic">mythopoeic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87920728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7026401975434374398"><b>Update 3/10/2017</b> Sadly, after reading YA for almost a decade now, I see that Megan Whalen Turner still remains almost the only author who puts sophisticated political intrigue into her fantasy books for kids. <br/><br/>BUT the wait for her next Thief book is almost over!<br/><br/><b>Original review</b><br/>I love, love this series and I am now very sad that after reading this 4th book I must wait another 3-5 years for the next one to be published! I guess I will have to ease the pain of separation by re-reading all 4 installme</span>
  <span id="freeText7026401975434374398" style="display:none"><b>Update 3/10/2017</b> Sadly, after reading YA for almost a decade now, I see that Megan Whalen Turner still remains almost the only author who puts sophisticated political intrigue into her fantasy books for kids. <br /><br />BUT the wait for her next Thief book is almost over!<br /><br /><b>Original review</b><br />I love, love this series and I am now very sad that after reading this 4th book I must wait another 3-5 years for the next one to be published! I guess I will have to ease the pain of separation by re-reading all 4 installments some time soon. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527841.A_Conspiracy_of_Kings__The_Queen_s_Thief___4_" title="A Conspiracy of Kings (The Queen's Thief, #4) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conspiracy of Kings</a> is most and foremost Sophos's story. I will not give anything away by saying that it is a book about his ascend to the throne of Sounis. And of course, the road to power is hard and full of obstacles.<br /><br />The story is told primarily from Sophos's 1st person POV. He narrates the 1st and 3rd part of the story. The 2nd part is told in 3rd person. I just love how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> plays with POVs, always finding new interesting ways to show the events and relationships from different angles.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527841.A_Conspiracy_of_Kings__The_Queen_s_Thief___4_" title="A Conspiracy of Kings (The Queen's Thief, #4) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conspiracy of Kings</a> is absolutely on par with Turner's previous books - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40159.The_King_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___3_" title="The King of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #3) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The King of Attolia</a>. Many reviewers complain that this book is not as good because Eugenides is just a secondary character in it, but I disagree. I love Gen and his sneaky ways, but I enjoy the books because of the outstanding writing, skillful world-building and intricate political intrigues. All of it is present in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527841.A_Conspiracy_of_Kings__The_Queen_s_Thief___4_" title="A Conspiracy of Kings (The Queen's Thief, #4) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conspiracy of Kings</a>, plus another never-easy romance. And Sophos is an interesting narrator too. He is very unlike Eugenides and his insecurities and humbleness make his road to power ever so much more compelling. <br /><br />An excellent addition to <i>The Queen's Thief</i> series and a must read for all <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> fans. I wonder what else she has in store for us. Will Eddis, Sounis and Attolia have to take on Mede? The danger of Mede invasion is always looming. And what is the fate of Eddis? Its future looks rather bleak at the moment...</span>
  <a data-text-id="7026401975434374398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2183020384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2183020384" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2183020384?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062642998" href="/book/show/30363362-a-conspiracy-of-kings">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=ya-fantasy-sci-fi">ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2183020384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1453141777174748528">4.5 ⭐️ (for that ending.)<br/><br/>I love this series so damn much.<br/><br/>But, needless to say, that at first, I was very reluctant and fearful to start this book because, well... how would you feel if told that the brilliant hero of one of your favourite series will take a back seat, so that others may step in? Because the fact is, Eugenides (Gen) MAKES this series. Of course, along with its brilliant writing. <br/>Every book with him in it is like an adventure you never want to end (I’m STILL melancholic from compl</span>
  <span id="freeText1453141777174748528" style="display:none">4.5 ⭐️ (for that ending.)<br /><br />I love this series so damn much.<br /><br />But, needless to say, that at first, I was very reluctant and fearful to start this book because, well... how would you feel if told that the brilliant hero of one of your favourite series will take a back seat, so that others may step in? Because the fact is, Eugenides (Gen) MAKES this series. Of course, along with its brilliant writing. <br />Every book with him in it is like an adventure you never want to end (I’m STILL melancholic from completing the King of Attolia). When he’s in his element - cunning, deceiving, brilliantly throwing everyone off their game and pulling the rug right from under them is seriously what makes me look forward to each of these books. So, do imagine my fear and reluctance. <br /><br />A Conspiracy of Kings is Sophos’ book. The focus of the story shifts from Eugenides to Sophos and literally tells his coming of age story. <br />We were first introduced to Sophos, the reluctant heir to the kingdom of Sounis in The Thief and became Gen’s friend, only to disappear during the events of The Queen of Attolia. And in this book, we learn all about his journey and his many trials, as he goes from a soft-hearted, timid boy, to a slave, to King. <br />In the space of one short book, Sophos goes through some serious character development as he learns the harsh realities of being an heir to a throne and the responsibilities it bears.<br /><br />plot-wise, it is still as politically driven as its predecessors with plenty of deceit, manipulative antics and lots of plots and counterplots. <br /><br />Structure-wise, the book is split into two narrative modes. The first and last parts of the story are told in the first person by Sophos and middle part in the third person by a narrator (The section which includes Gen). If you feel scepticism coming your way, ignore it because it all weaves in together beautifully, with a great sense of interconnectivity. <br /><br />All in all, as much as I loved Sophos, it was ultimately Gen who once again sucked me into the story as he still managed to craft one heck of a masterful plan without even having that much presence at all. Which really is a testament to Turner’s writing skills.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1453141777174748528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2084627754" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2084627754" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2084627754?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062642998" href="/book/show/30363362-a-conspiracy-of-kings">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">At this point I don't know what to say. YOU.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2084627754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11536670919653393439"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502239958i/23538289._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Look, <b>I'm not going to beat about the bush</b> : <i>yes</i>, I know that the relative absence of Eugenides as an explanation for my rating is ridiculous. I objectively, honestly <i>know</i> that. Now, does that change <i>in any way</i> the fact that my heart is ridiculous by essence, because that's what hearts do, right, falling in love, breaking, and so on, as the unruly little shits they are? Well, <b>no.</b> <br/><br/>I can stress <br/>a) how captivating <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527841.A_Conspiracy_of_Kings__The_Queen_s_Thief___4_' title='A Conspiracy of Kings (The Queen's Thief, #4) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Conspiracy of Kings</a> is ; <br/>b) how brilliantly <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner' title='Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>Megan Whalen Turner</a> handles the POVs ; </span>
  <span id="freeText11536670919653393439" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502239958i/23538289._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Look, <b>I'm not going to beat about the bush</b> : <i>yes</i>, I know that the relative absence of Eugenides as an explanation for my rating is ridiculous. I objectively, honestly <i>know</i> that. Now, does that change <i>in any way</i> the fact that my heart is ridiculous by essence, because that's what hearts do, right, falling in love, breaking, and so on, as the unruly little shits they are? Well, <b>no.</b> <br><br>I can stress <br>a) how captivating <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527841.A_Conspiracy_of_Kings__The_Queen_s_Thief___4_" title="A Conspiracy of Kings (The Queen's Thief, #4) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conspiracy of Kings</a> is ; <br>b) how brilliantly <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> handles the POVs ; <br>c) how endearing and interesting Sophos is (and his growth! Awesome stuff here, I'm telling you!) <br><br>(we could go all day, but I'll choose not to, if that's okay with you)<br><br>... having said all that, I can't ignore that I didn't enjoy it as much as I did books 2 and 3, and I very much believe that it's because Eugenides' interactions and tricks are necessary for me to give it a full 5. Sophos <i>is</i> a very good character, but <b>he lacks Gen's spark.</b><br> <br>¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br><br>HOWEVER, <b>let's not make it seem as if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527841.A_Conspiracy_of_Kings__The_Queen_s_Thief___4_" title="A Conspiracy of Kings (The Queen's Thief, #4) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conspiracy of Kings</a> wasn't an amazing YA Fantasy novel, alright?</b> Because just thinking about what that genre offers us 99% of the time, there's no forgetting that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> has <i>by far</i> the upper hand over <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5295120.Morgan_Rhodes" title="Morgan Rhodes" rel="nofollow noopener">Morgan Rhodes</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3433047.Sarah_J__Maas" title="Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah J. Maas</a> or even - and I do love them - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/125308.Cinda_Williams_Chima" title="Cinda Williams Chima" rel="nofollow noopener">Cinda Williams Chima</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995873.Julie_Kagawa" title="Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Kagawa</a>. By the way, I saw readers shelving these novels as middle-grade, and I wonder... Is that because there's no sex scenes, even fade-to-black? No, I have to ask, because I genuinely do not understand what's so childish about <b>intricate conspiracies, complex characters, a writing very engaging, blurred lines between good and evil</b> - there's no such thing as a moustache-twisting villain in these books, but rather, complicated human beings who make the choices they think are best... Perhaps I am deluded about what <i>is</i> Middle-Grade and what it is not, but please enlighten me? Or maybe not, as I'm quite convinced that I wouldn't agree with you. So there's that.<br> <br><blockquote>
  <i>"Then I walked to my bed and sat, making a show of careless bravado by crossing my legs and slumping as if I had not a worry in the world. In other words, I gave my best imitation of Eugenides."</i>
</blockquote><br>Anyway, as usual with series, I won't rehash the plot because<br>1) You may not have read the other books, and would probably burn me at a stake if I spoiled you, and we wouldn't want that, would we?<br>2) I <i>tend</i> to repeat myself in these cases and I assure you that you don't want to be on the receiving end of my disheveled rambling when this series is concerned. Trust me. Or no, better : ask my friends. <br><br>On a final note : Yes, every one of Eugenides' apparitions gave me life, and I'm almost certain that would I reread <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527841.A_Conspiracy_of_Kings__The_Queen_s_Thief___4_" title="A Conspiracy of Kings (The Queen's Thief, #4) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conspiracy of Kings</a> later, I'd probably give out a 5 stars rating. <br><br>For now, I'll have to accept that I am <i>not</i> an objective reviewer. <br><br>*snorts* <br><br>As if it existed. <br><br>PS. I'm including my favorite quote under a spoiler tag for those of you who have read it. I just couldn't <i>not</i> XD<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<blockquote><i>"Then, as you well know, Eugenides looked me in the eye as if i were a complete stranger and said, "The simplest way to end a war is to admit you have lost it.<br>The silence after that was not polite."</i></blockquote>
<br>I must be an awful human being because I laughed. So. HARD. I just adore the way Gen always surprises me. It's a full-time job and he's the best at it XD <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>PS <i>bis</i>. I'm diving headfirst into an horrible book hangover, am I not? I will never learn, it seems. Sigh.<br><br><u>My reviews for the other books of the series</u> : <br>۩ Book 1, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237053624" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> ★★★★ <br>۩ Book 2, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2082723668" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> ★★★★ 1/2<br>۩ Book 3, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2083617029?type=review#rating_127283259" rel="nofollow noopener">The King of Attolia</a> ★★★★★ [ONE OF THE BEST BOOKS I'VE EVER READ]<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>

<div id="review_59487245" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59487245" />
    <a title="Mir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/237469-mir"><img alt="Mir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275489063p2/237469.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/59487245?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mir" href="/user/show/237469-mir">Mir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/237469-mir?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59487245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5801224362713151295">Engrossing, but I didn't love it the way I loved the previous three volumes of the series. It lacked the liveliness and humor that characterized the other books. In some ways, that made sense -- Sophos is kind and sincere person rather than a clever and adventurous one. In a natural progression from the third volume, this focused more on external politics and the ethical dilemmas of rule. Those are important and Turner handles them with delicacy. But I missed the funny!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160645929" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160645929" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160645929?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160645929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4937791454037811668">After attempting to organize my thoughts about this book for about an hour and making no progress at all, I decided to throw in the towel and go to bed. Of course, once I got there and lay down, my brain would just not shut up about what it wants to write about this book (Oh, so <i>now</i> you’re talking, eh? Bastard.). So, I am giving in. This better not be a fake-out, brain.<br/><br/>I am so consistently surprised and impressed by this series as it progresses. <u>A Conspiracy of Kings</u> is definitely a favorite, se</span>
  <span id="freeText4937791454037811668" style="display:none">After attempting to organize my thoughts about this book for about an hour and making no progress at all, I decided to throw in the towel and go to bed. Of course, once I got there and lay down, my brain would just not shut up about what it wants to write about this book (Oh, so <i>now</i> you’re talking, eh? Bastard.). So, I am giving in. This better not be a fake-out, brain.<br /><br />I am so consistently surprised and impressed by this series as it progresses. <u>A Conspiracy of Kings</u> is definitely a favorite, second only to <u>The Queen of Attolia.</u><br /><br />Sophos is first introduced in <u>The Thief</u>, where he is a young and somewhat guileless student of the Magus of Sounis. He grudgingly reveals that he is the heir of Sounis, but it’s clear that he much prefers a scholarly life of poetry and philosophy. He is a place-holder heir, maneuvered into the position by his scheming father, and waiting to be replaced by his uncle’s first born. When he shows no talent for leadership, he is banished to live with his mother and sisters and a string of unwanted tutors. In <u>The King of Attolia</u>, it is revealed that he has been abducted and is possibly dead. This book begins with that abduction, and follows Sophos through all of the twists of fate, moral dilemmas, and hard choices that will lead him to be a King.<br /><br />I have seen some lament the absence of Eugenides in this book, but to me he is still <i>palpable.</i> I can feel his grief and conflict so strongly, as he is once again required to make a performance for the benefit of all. I love the few tender moments where we get to witness the affection between Eugenides and Attolia. I don’t know how Megan Whalen Turner does it, but she has managed to create two of my favorite literary romances, within the span of only a few pages out of about a thousand. At nearly the end of this book I was thinking, “I guess there’s not very much romance in this one.” Then, bam, I get to page 303 and suddenly I love this relationship. What she has created, that is so incredibly spectacular, are two couples that consist of absolute equals. It sounds so simple, but I rarely see romance with partners coming together on such equal footing. One of my favorite parts of this book is when Eugenides realizes that if he ever falls out of favor with his wife, no amount of planning could ever save him from her wrath. For some weird reason, that seems very romantic to me.<br /><br />Megan Whalen Turner once again uses differing points of view to great effect. In <u>The Queen of Attolia</u> we were distanced from Eugenides and the Queen by a third person point of view and even more so in <u>The King of Attolia</u>, where we followed a minor character with a third person point of view. This perspective so deftly captures the natures of Eugenides and Attolia: they are hidden and calculating, and what we can’t see is just as important as what we can. With Eugenides, his public persona is so often a charade. In this book, a first person point of view is used primarily, except for small sections in the middle and the end (when Eugenides and the Queen are involved…). Sophos is incapable of lying convincingly and he has high, noble ideals. This perspective fits his character so perfectly, as he uses plain truth and his own real emotions to maneuver around his enemies (and I love the little "reveal" on page 132).<br /><br />I love the moral dilemmas and questions posed by this book. Sophos learns about what kind of leader he wants to be, and he has a grand vision, but his country is strained by feuding and betrayal, encouraged by the former King. I didn’t expect the choice that Sophos eventually makes, and it was intense. There is a lot to think about here – about what is morally right, and what is required, and that eventual peace sometimes necessitates violence. I love this quote from Eddis:<br /><br /><i>”We are not philosophers; we are sovereigns. The rules that govern our behavior are not the rules for other men, and our honor, I think, is a different thing entirely, difficult for anyone but the historians and the gods to judge.”</i><br /><br />All I can say is that I have grown very attached to these characters, and I am sad to have to say goodbye to them, for what will probably be quite some time. I hope that Megan Whalen Turner eventually explores the Medeans more thoroughly, as she has done with all of the previous villains. I think that I can trust that she will not leave them to be simplistic, black enemies.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4937791454037811668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_826598806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826598806" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826598806?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826598806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16299553101511061598">This is the fourth book in the fantastic THIEF historical fantasy series, but the first one in which Eugenides isn’t front and center, and Gen is sadly missed by both me and the main character, Sophos. Still, it’s an interesting and thoughtful tale with (of course) a few great twists up its sleeves.<br/><br/>Sophos, a young man in the royal family of Sounis, is unexpectedly attacked in his villa, along with his family. He’s able to evade his attackers, but one thing leads to another and Sophos ends up bei</span>
  <span id="freeText16299553101511061598" style="display:none">This is the fourth book in the fantastic THIEF historical fantasy series, but the first one in which Eugenides isn’t front and center, and Gen is sadly missed by both me and the main character, Sophos. Still, it’s an interesting and thoughtful tale with (of course) a few great twists up its sleeves.<br /><br />Sophos, a young man in the royal family of Sounis, is unexpectedly attacked in his villa, along with his family. He’s able to evade his attackers, but one thing leads to another and Sophos ends up being sold into slavery, which is at least better than being murdered. It’s a rough adjustment for the once-soft young man, though he’s actually happier without the pressures and expectations of royal life. Gradually he’s able to make friends among the slaves and finds himself reasonably contented with his new life. But life, or fate, or the gods, have more in mind for Sophos.<br /><br />It’s a solid coming-of-age story in an Ancient Greece-like setting. This one’s a soft 4 stars for me, but overall this is an amazingly good series that shouldn’t be missed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16299553101511061598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1354489565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1354489565" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1354489565?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1354489565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14301300694677348976">Buddy Read with some series fanatics at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books & Baubles</a> <br/><br/>Every once and awhile I like to jump into some Middle Grade reading. They can be a lot of fun and full of great stories that I don’t have to really focus completely on to enjoy as an adult. This is one of those MG stories that I’ve read and thought I really would love it if this was an Adult Fantasy instead. It is written mostly about adults or young adults becoming more than they thought they could be, but I would have loved a more</span>
  <span id="freeText14301300694677348976" style="display:none">Buddy Read with some series fanatics at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books &amp; Baubles</a> <br /><br />Every once and awhile I like to jump into some Middle Grade reading. They can be a lot of fun and full of great stories that I don’t have to really focus completely on to enjoy as an adult. This is one of those MG stories that I’ve read and thought I really would love it if this was an Adult Fantasy instead. It is written mostly about adults or young adults becoming more than they thought they could be, but I would have loved a more in depth adult version of this story just for the character interactions.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>All my life they had made choices for me, and I had resented it. Now the choice was mine, and once it was made, I would have no right to blame anyone else for the consequences. Loss of that privilege, to blame others, unexpectedly stung</i>
</blockquote><br />Sophos is the heir of Sounis and has known that his entire life. He has never wanted to be king, in fact he always believed he’d be happier as a poet or scholar. Sophos has been a disappointment to both his uncle the current King of Sounis and father most of his life. He has done all he can not to be heirlike for as long as he has been alive with small personal rebellions. But that was before, before the current king died and before the rebels stole him from his home intending to make him a puppet king.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>”A lamb, they said. No more trouble than snatching up a little lamb.” </i>
</blockquote><br />But Sophos has spent time with the King of Attolia, the former Thief of Eddis and he is not so easy to puppet and will channel all the monarchs he has known to be able to thwart the plans they have in store for him.<br /><br />Even though this story focuses on Sophos I was so glad to see how Gen contributed to the story and how much he has taught and is teaching Sophos, even when Sophos isn’t aware that is what he is doing. Gen is still sneaky that way, you never really know what game he is playing. Even when Gen pretends to be weak he is still strong and plotting something extraordinary. I love the relationship between Gen and Sophos even though they are both Kings of different countries they care for each other greatly.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> Eddis did not say what she was thinking: that Sophos held Gen’s heart in his hand, that he was one of very few people who could destroy the king of Attolia, and that Attolia knew it.</i>
</blockquote><br />But beyond watching Sophos come into his own as a man and a king who is fighting to regain the reigns of his country I really liked the budding love story between Eddis and Sophos. How they had to figure out how to be the monarchs they are and still find a way to create a happy union between their two kingdoms. The romance is very subdued because of the Middle Gradeness of the story but it was still tender and sweet in spots.<br /><br />Overall The King Of Attolia was my favorite book of this series so far but I did enjoy this one nearly as much and look forward to what the next book in the story could be about.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14301300694677348976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/998274757?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaethe Douglas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaethe Douglas" href="/user/show/1072582-kaethe-douglas">Kaethe Douglas</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=feminism">feminism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=libraries">libraries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=swashbuckling">swashbuckling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998274757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2112632156707026328">June 28, 2012<br/><br/>You know what Lewis left out of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100915.The_Lion__the_Witch_and_the_Wardrobe__Chronicles_of_Narnia___1_' title='The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe (Chronicles of Narnia, #1) by C.S. Lewis' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</a>? Ruling. He draws four human children in to rule his magical world of talking animals and mythical human/creature hybrids, makes them kings and queens and then elides over a decade or so before throwing them back into childish bodies in a war zone. Certainly when I was nine I didn't get hung up on what it would entail, being a queen, nor did I worry about humans being in charge of a society of non-humans, nor did </span>
  <span id="freeText2112632156707026328" style="display:none">June 28, 2012<br /><br />You know what Lewis left out of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100915.The_Lion__the_Witch_and_the_Wardrobe__Chronicles_of_Narnia___1_" title="The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe (Chronicles of Narnia, #1) by C.S. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</a>? Ruling. He draws four human children in to rule his magical world of talking animals and mythical human/creature hybrids, makes them kings and queens and then elides over a decade or so before throwing them back into childish bodies in a war zone. Certainly when I was nine I didn't get hung up on what it would entail, being a queen, nor did I worry about humans being in charge of a society of non-humans, nor did I worry about having to grow up once and then go back and do it again. Now that horrifies me: growing up and ruling a country and then having to go back to being seven in elementary school again? Like I didn't have enough smart-assery the first time through? I fought a war and saved a nation and now I have to sit quietly in a classroom doing multiplication work sheets? I was queen and now I have to hold my hand up and hope the teacher grants me permission to pee?<br /><br />Sorry, I got sidetracked by the horror. Anyway, that is what makes The Queen's Thief series so awesome: the consideration of what it is that a king or queen does. How, as a young ruler, do you convince people to listen to you? How do you bring contentious and patronizing older people around to your side? That her characters just happen to have the minds of chess masters when it comes to politics makes the solution amusingly clever.<br /><br />Great stuff, utterly engrossing, full of derring-do, but with a realistic-seeming portrayal of what court life would really be like. I suggest that everyone keep a set of these books packed and ready to go at the back of every wardrobe, just in case. <br /><br />Library copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2112632156707026328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_105145520" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105145520" />
    <a title="Lightreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads"><img alt="Lightreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230606449p2/1836077.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105145520?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lightreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lightreads" href="/user/show/1836077-lightreads">Lightreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=disability">disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105145520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2472745999292301101">So feel free to jump in and tell me if I get any of this wrong, but I <i>think</i> the way this works is I read a book for pleasure and then I talk about it. It’s the “for pleasure” that’s really throwing me.<br/><br/>I read <i>this</i> book two months and the bar exam ago, and I don’t actually have a lot to say about it. Young adult fantasy politics series that makes me flail and emit high-pitched noises. These are books that are not nearly as young as they pretend to be. They are about violence and disability and tak</span>
  <span id="freeText2472745999292301101" style="display:none">So feel free to jump in and tell me if I get any of this wrong, but I <i>think</i> the way this works is I read a book for pleasure and then I talk about it. It’s the “for pleasure” that’s really throwing me.<br /><br />I read <i>this</i> book two months and the bar exam ago, and I don’t actually have a lot to say about it. Young adult fantasy politics series that makes me flail and emit high-pitched noises. These are books that are not nearly as young as they pretend to be. They are about violence and disability and taking responsibility for your actions and getting hurt and getting better. And being clever and awesome and causing trouble.<br /><br />This book is not as awesome as the last two. Nothing really <i>wrong</i> with it, though the romance is a bit, “and they entered the arc two-by-two,” if you know what I mean. I think my problem is that this is a transitional book, moving several key pieces across the board. Fine, but I realized why I have been mentally categorizing this series as I have: like Francis Crawford of Lymond, Miles Vorkosigan, and Peter Wimsey, the intense personal charisma of the series protagonist overwhelms everything else, so even when other characters are awesome, they only really exist to me in their relationship to him. And this book was only a little bit about that.<br /><br />Next book, please and thank you. And the one after that, since you’re up.<br /></span>

<div id="review_63789974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63789974" />
    <a title="Sherwood Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/162084-sherwood-smith"><img alt="Sherwood Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543007644p2/162084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63789974?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sherwood Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sherwood Smith" href="/user/show/162084-sherwood-smith">Sherwood Smith</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162084-sherwood-smith?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer63789974&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63789974" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17712195408195857888">Initial reaction: I continue to wonder how many actual teens read these books; I tend to think that structure and emotional as well as political subtext are most enjoyable for older readers. That's just an observation, it's in no way a criticism.<br/><br/>Okay, I finished--and as always, admire the vivid writing, the wry humor, and how superlative Turner's storytelling abilities are.<br/><br/>At one crucial point I had to stop and reread the first three. As always I admired the graceful, witty writing, the vivid im</span>
  <span id="freeText17712195408195857888" style="display:none">Initial reaction: I continue to wonder how many actual teens read these books; I tend to think that structure and emotional as well as political subtext are most enjoyable for older readers. That's just an observation, it's in no way a criticism.<br /><br />Okay, I finished--and as always, admire the vivid writing, the wry humor, and how superlative Turner's storytelling abilities are.<br /><br />At one crucial point I had to stop and reread the first three. As always I admired the graceful, witty writing, the vivid imagery, the fine characterization.<br /><br />A general observation first, which is a kind of caveat: <i>Queen</i> had seemed a transitional novel to me, in a way; when <i>King</i> came out, I thought, ah, there is the second half.<br /><br /><i>A Conspiracy of Kings</i> perhaps might be a transitional novel, setting up questions and not answering them, though it might seem we've been given answers. <br /><br />The structure is unusual: the first third or so, Sophos in captivity, is terrifically told and paced. The next third shifts into a great deal of expositional mode as complicated off-stage politics are sifted in. I thought Turner did a fine job with Sophos' emotional frustration as pretty much all the action is out of his view. The last third is action again, with a surprise that perhaps isn't that surprising if the reader knows Gen.<br /><br />So here comes my spoiler discussion.<br /><br />I had to stop in this segment and reread because there was a subtext that disturbed me increasingly. Perhaps the reader is being set up for bigger stakes, and bigger costs (it was easy to imagine an enemy being lured up to a volcano just before it explodes, for example) and the characters for bigger falls, but this book repeatedly had our young kings and queens reminded, or reminding themselves, that loss of subjects' lives is to be expected. Part of kingship--you gotta man up if you're to rule. You can't worry about those who died in carrying out your will.<br /><br />I don't think I need to point out the obvious political parallels, but they hit me hard enough that I had to go back and reread the books. In <i>The Thief</i>, when Gen kills, he is hit hard by remorse, he gives a thought to the dead, he is aware of the cost of his temper and his skills when employed in violence. With each succeeding book, he reacts less; in this one, we do see Gen get dumped on his backside once or twice, but other than that he'd become a distant manipulator--wry, witty, and human to those few he lets close. Otherwise he's become a basileus--which I find a bit less interesting. In a lesser writer, he might have dwindled to a Marty Stu. Turner is far too good for that--he's still Gen--but I didn't find him nearly as compelling a character, but that caused another disturbing thought: Gen has always been most heroic when he's physically suffering the most.<br /><br />Sophos wants to be Gen; when he decides he has to kill, there is no moment of reaction, and when he chooses the most bloody course . . . well, that's what tough kings and queens <i>do</i>.<br /><br />So at the end of the fourth book, being an adult reader, I have this question in mind: The Medes have become an evil "them" . . . but is the cost of building the three lands in order to resist being conquered turning our heroes into their likenesses?<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17712195408195857888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82869423" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82869423" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50378-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510342996p2/50378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82869423?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/50378-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=belovedbookshelf">belovedbookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=e-p-i-c">e-p-i-c</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82869423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12849255750447754537">I figured we should start the new year out right. And what better way to do that than with a review of what is quite possibly my most anticipated title of 2010? Thanks to my lovely book fairy and the benevolent folks at Greenwillow, I was the giddy recipient of a coveted ARC of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner' title='Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>Megan Whalen Turner</a>'s upcoming A CONSPIRACY OF KINGS. For those not in the know, this is the fourth novel in the spectacular Queen's Thief series. The series that effectively robbed me of the ability to form coherent thou</span>
  <span id="freeText12849255750447754537" style="display:none">I figured we should start the new year out right. And what better way to do that than with a review of what is quite possibly my most anticipated title of 2010? Thanks to my lovely book fairy and the benevolent folks at Greenwillow, I was the giddy recipient of a coveted ARC of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a>'s upcoming A CONSPIRACY OF KINGS. For those not in the know, this is the fourth novel in the spectacular Queen's Thief series. The series that effectively robbed me of the ability to form coherent thoughts and/or sentences last February. The series that cast a complete spell over me and whose praises I have felt compelled to sing ever since. The series Ana and I had more than one spontaneous Twitter lovefest over. The series that was, hands down, my best discovery of 2009. So. Here we go.<br /><br />Sophos has had it rough since parting ways with his old friend Gen after the adventures of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19063.The_Book_Thief" title="The Book Thief by Markus Zusak" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> and their narrow escape from the Queen of Attolia's dungeon. In fact, things have gone rather downhill from there for the reluctant heir to the throne of Sounis. Having once again disappointed his father by preferring poetry and philosophy to politics and strategy, Sophos finds himself tutorless and packed off home in disgrace. But when an unidentified armed force storms his family's estate, his mother and sisters disappear and Sophos himself is abducted and sold into slavery. And suddenly the choice of whether or not to take up the mantle of his responsibilities is taken out of his hands and he is able to exist in blissful anonymity, doing manual labor building walls during the day and entertaining his fellow laborers with epic poems and tales around the fire at night. But life will not hold still for Sophos and even he can't fool himself into believing he can watch his country tear itself apart and not want to fight to save it. And so he chooses to fight and to step into the role he's been dreading his whole life. And when it comes to intrigue and subterfuge and playing a part, Sophos knows just the person he can call on.<br /><br />There is nothing like reading a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener"> Megan Whalen Turner</a> book. I mean nothing. You open the book to that first page and you just feel so at peace. Don't get me wrong, you're filled with an almost unbearable paroxysm of anticipation, joy, and anxiety on behalf of these characters you've come to care about so much it's almost a surprise to remember they're not real and you've never met. But you feel at peace, secure in the knowledge that everything is going to play out so beautifully, so perfectly, so achingly subtle, that there's no fear on your part. It's an unmatched reading experience and one to be treasured and taken out on cold nights and experienced all over again. I knew I was going to fall in love with Sophos in this volume. He was clearly so full of potential in book one, a few tantalizing hints here and there, and then he disappeared so utterly that I knew when he did come back, he would come back with a vengeance. And so he does. And so does Gen. And they're all four there in their Sounisian, Eddisian, and Attolian individuality and awesomeness and I quite honestly found it difficult not to stand up and applaud after reading each scene where they're talking or plotting or just sending each other meaningful glances and thinly veiled threats. Which, of course, is kind of every five pages or so. And I tried, I tried to stay on top of things, marking who was scheming what and which hidden motivations belonged to whom. And still, still they all surprised me! Which, of course, is exactly the way I hoped it would be. And the ending? The ending is perfect. The kind of perfect that makes me smile and clasp the book to my chest. <br /><br />I fretted over which bit to quote for you here. I couldn't not select just one passage to give you a glimpse into what we're dealing with here with Sophos. And so I chose a small scene fairly early on that contains no spoilers except, perhaps, for The Thief. So if you haven't read the first book, definitely skip this bit, which is taken from the uncorrected ARC. Otherwise, enjoy.<br /> <blockquote>When we were adventuring after Hamiathes's Gift, I had watched the magus beat Eugenides. We'd thought he was no more than a common thief named Gen from Sounis's gutters, and had listened to him whine and complain for days. When food was missing, it was easy to blame him. The magus used a riding crop on his back, and holy sacrificial lambs, Gen had come up off the ground like he'd been catapulted. It was as if he was a different person, some stranger who'd manifested in Gen's body. He'd dumped Pol flat onto his back--something I never thought I'd see--and gone for the magus. If Pol hadn't been up again so quickly, the magus was ready to run and dignity be damned. Even with Pol between him and Gen, the magus had been wary.<br /><br /> I thought later that this was the real Gen revealed, the person who'd been hiding behind a screen of complaints and needling humor. But I spent whole days with Eugenides after our adventures, and that Eugenides was exactly the Gen I had traveled with. Maybe I don't know which Gen is real. But I know there was nothing feigned about his emotions after he had been beaten.<br /><br /> Where, I wondered, was my wounded pride? Where was my outrage? My self-respect? Nowhere, it seemed. My back hurt. I lay there on my pallet, hoping it would improve soon and wondering, in a distant, unreproachful sort of way, if I was any kind of man at all and decided that I probably wasn't.</blockquote><br />Oh, Sophos. You are so earnest and self-deprecating and you have a good heart. I loved making this journey with you.<br /><br />A CONSPIRACY OF KINGS is due out March 23rd.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12849255750447754537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2814315722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2814315722" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2814315722?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2814315722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4934849861122003724">This 4th book in Megan Whalen Turner's <i>Queen's Thief</i> series was not quite as good as the excellent third instalment of the series but it was still an enjoyable and worthwhile read in its own right. Like the rest of the books in this series this was an intelligent YA fantasy with a heavy focus on characters and intrigue. <br/><br/>I liked the fact that this book told the story of Sophos, the heir of Sounis, who went missing in the third book in the series. I always liked the character so was delighted we f</span>
  <span id="freeText4934849861122003724" style="display:none">This 4th book in Megan Whalen Turner's <i>Queen's Thief</i> series was not quite as good as the excellent third instalment of the series but it was still an enjoyable and worthwhile read in its own right. Like the rest of the books in this series this was an intelligent YA fantasy with a heavy focus on characters and intrigue. <br /><br />I liked the fact that this book told the story of Sophos, the heir of Sounis, who went missing in the third book in the series. I always liked the character so was delighted we finally got his story and ended up mostly happy with the way it played out. Turner always does an excellent job with the plots of these books and I love how even seemingly throwaway scenes always end up having some sort of significance! <br /><br />If this book had a flaw it was in the set up. A lot of this was Sophos telling his own story, which was good because it gave us his tale from his POV, but it was also an issue as the set-up of it meant we had two phases of the story where Sophos was telling someone his story. That flashback set-up killed a bit of the tension since we knew where Sophos ended up by the end of both parts of the story! I'd have preferred just a straight chronological tale from the point of view of Sophos as I feel like that would have added more tension and uncertainty to the tale. I love first person POV but am not keen on flashbacks as a storytelling tool as it almost always kills the tension. This story was enjoyable despite the fact that the set up hindered it a bit. <br /><br />As always some of the things the characters did annoyed me but by the time we reached the end of the tale I was left mostly satisfied as we eventually learned why the characters made the choices they did over the course of the story. <br /><br />The one other thing that annoyed me was Turner using time Sophos spent as a slave as a way to show he was enjoying a break from the life of the pressures and responsibilities of being the King's heir. I've had moments like this happen in a few of my books in the last year or two and it always annoys me and leaves me feeling the author comes from a privileged background and is completely detached from the true realities of a life of poverty and hardship. There are better ways to show a character is enjoying a break from the pressure of their old lives than painting slavery or homelessness as a fun break! <br /><br />I seems I've wrote a lot of negatives in this review but the weird thing is I was mostly happy with the story and did quite enjoy it. I look forward to reading the next book in the series.<br /><br />Rating: 3.5 stars. I'm rounding up as it was close to getting 4 stars anyway.<br /><br />Audio Note: As always Jeff Woodman did a great job with the audio. Pity he was not retained to read the rest of the books in the series as he always does an excellent job. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4934849861122003724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
